  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f01e6375-4231-4f55-80bc-2e57390013a7'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText4551908905672908444" style="display:none">NEW YORK CITY AS YOU'VE NEVER SEEN IT BEFORE.<br /><br /><i>A thousand-story tower stretching into the sky. A glittering vision of the future where anything is possible—if you want it enough.</i><br /><br />WELCOME TO MANHATTAN, 2118.<br /><br />A hundred years in the future, New York is a city of innovation and dreams. Everyone there wants something…and everyone has something to lose.<br /><br />LEDA COLE’s flawless exterior belies a secret addiction—to a drug she never should have tried and a boy she never should have touched.<br /><br />ERIS DODD-RADSON’s beautiful, carefree life falls to pieces when a heartbreaking betrayal tears her family apart.<br /><br />RYLIN MYERS’s job on one of the highest floors sweeps her into a world—and a romance—she never imagined…but will this new life cost Rylin her old one?<br /><br />WATT BAKRADI is a tech genius with a secret: he knows everything about everyone. But when he’s hired to spy for an upper-floor girl, he finds himself caught up in a complicated web of lies.<br /><br />And living above everyone else on the thousandth floor is AVERY FULLER, the girl genetically designed to be perfect. The girl who seems to have it all—yet is tormented by the one thing she can never have.<br /><br />Amid breathtaking advancement and high-tech luxury, five teenagers struggle to find their place at the top of the world. But when you're this high up, there's nowhere to go but down....</span>

</div>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_853305'><a id="like_count_community_question_853305" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/853305?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F24921954-the-thousandth-floor">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/58997992-katherine-luca"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/58997992-katherine-luca">Katherine Luca</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are five different sex scenes, including a rape, although the book never describes it as rape, just "being tricked." I don't know why Marianne s<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are five different sex scenes, including a rape, although the book never describes it as rape, just "being tricked." I don't know why Marianne said there's no profanity, since I was actually shocked that this book got away with the amount of profanity used (three F-bombs, and the d and b-words are thrown around as well) There is a murder, but it's not in much detail. There is domestic abuse between two characters. There is also heavy substance abuse/underage drinking, as Marianne said. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1779351496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1779351496" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1779351496?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062418593" href="/book/show/28218953-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one. genuinely. </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2016">y-out2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=what-is-this-mess">what-is-this-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-scifi-dystopias">sff-scifi-dystopias</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1779351496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5849796836751334181">Wow.<br/><br/><i>The Thousandth Floor</i> is a <b>
  <u>futuristic Gossip Girl</u>
</b> which would be a lot more fun if not for the adopted sibling incest, worst case of bury your gays i have ever had the displeasure of seeing, and also eugenics. At around the halfway I was actually planning to give this a two-star rating, just based off how addictive it was and how much I personally enjoyed it. But given how much the ending pissed me off, and given that after over six months (update: almost four years) I despise this book m</span>
  <span id="freeText5849796836751334181" style="display:none">Wow.<br /><br /><i>The Thousandth Floor</i> is a <b>
  <u>futuristic Gossip Girl</u>
</b> which would be a lot more fun if not for the adopted sibling incest, worst case of bury your gays i have ever had the displeasure of seeing, and also eugenics. At around the halfway I was actually planning to give this a two-star rating, just based off how addictive it was and how much I personally enjoyed it. But given how much the ending pissed me off, and given that after over six months (update: almost four years) I despise this book more every time I think about it, I'm not at all planning on changing this rating. This book deserves its rating. <br /><br />You're all waiting for the roast, right? It's at the bottom. <br /><br />Okay, first of all, this isn't a cool dystopia; this book is about <b>
  <u>romantic drama.</u>
</b> Yes, there's a little worldbuilding, and it's interesting when we do see it. But the focus is on dating. Eris used to like Cord who likes Rylin, Avery and Leda like Atlas, but Watt also likes Avery. The only relationship I could bring myself to care about was <b>
  <u>Eris' relationship with Mariel,</u>
</b> which was genuine and led Eris through some GREAT development and then gets ruined because of course it does. Every other relationship felt like a plot point for drama. Cord and Rylin weren't a <i>horrible</i> couple either, but unfortunately, they were clearly there for the drama. Atlas and Avery creeped me out. <b>Look, I have a stepbrother. Siblings, even if they aren't biological, should not date.</b> Yuck.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>✔ GOSSIP GIRL HAD MORE CHARACTER DEPTH THAN THIS</u>
</b><br /><br />⭐ Avery, aka Cersei Lannister, is a virginal blonde girl who lives on the top floor, and she's utterly insufferable. Avery slutshames, talks shit about all her friends, and is ridiculously hateable. That's her entire character. I feel like she has a lot of potential as a delicious antihero, but she's not <i>portrayed</i> as an antihero - she's portrayed as an innocent. Also, she fucks her brother. Yeah.<br /><br />⭐ Watt is a stalker. That's his only character trait. Besides a few weirdly racial stereotypes. <br /><br />⭐ Leda... was a very frustrating character to follow. She begins the story as a former drug addict who's really trying to get clean and has some nice relationships with her mom and brother. She's loyal and into meditation, and really the only annoying bit about her is her dislike for Eris. She ends the book as a completely terrible person with no character whatsoever. Leda's character arc feels <b>
  <u>messy at best and false at worst.</u>
</b> You deserved better, Leda. She, too, has a lot of potential as a delicious antihero, but she's not <i>portrayed</i> as an antihero - she's the villain. <br /><br />⭐ Rylin is very protective of her sister, Chrissa, and is less rich than the rest - she lives on 32. Her character is a bit of a cliche, poor because her mother is dead, but she's less whiny than the rich kids. She had potential. HOWEVER. Rylin's character development is not positive, and she's reduced almost entirely to <b>
  <u>her bland romance plot.</u>
</b><br /><br />⭐ Eris annoyed me a lot at the beginning, but she grew on me. She is forced to live down on the bottom levels by a family tragedy, and her relationship with her parents was relatively well-developed. Erin is also the only character that really develops, which is like... sad.<br /><br />To some degree this book is enjoyable in that "mindless drama" sort of way. It's just too bad it was so, so problematic and angering. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>✔ THIS BOOK IS YIKES AND IN CONCLUSION: I AM BITTER</u>
</b><br /><br />♚ While I loved Eris as a character, it should be noted that she's stereotyped too - it's time for us to end the trope of <b>
  <u>the one bisexual character who "sleeps around" and almost cheats.</u>
</b><br /><br />♔ <b>
  <u>Soooooooo much girl hate and slutshaming.</u>
</b> Oh god, there was so much girl hate in this book in general. Aside from Eris and Mariel, who are dating, there is not one positive relationship between women, and worse, most of the issues in these friendships revolve around guys or slutshaming. This is just annoying. It's 2017. We can have normal friendships. <br /><br />♚ Women are treated like sex objects and no one really does anything about it. You guys think I'm kidding. At one point, a male characters slaps a female character's ass - they are not dating - and it is literally just considered a flirty gesture <i>by the girl</i>. This is really just objectively shitty worldbuilding; we're living in 2150, and you're telling me treating girls like meat is still okay?<br /><br />♔ Pretty much all the dude love interests are somewhat hypermasculine and vaguely creepy in my reading. I <i>think</i> I'm supposed to want Atlas and Avery together, but honestly, their relationship read as somewhat... creepy... to me. And not even just because they're siblings [oh yeah, they're siblings] but Atlas is just a fucking creeper. He reads like every 30-year-old who's ever hit on me at the gym.<br /><br />♚ Rape was treated somewhat badly, at least in my reading. There's also something that happens at the end of this book where it's implied one character daterapes another character and it's fairly glossed over. It's possible that this was <i>meant</i> to be horrifying and will be handled better in book two; that being said, to me it came across as "it's not real rape because it's a dude." <br /><br />♔ Some kind of... racial stereotyping. Yikes. One character is described as Middle Eastern, and has three character traits: socially awkward, computer nerd, and either can't get laid or is desperately trying to get laid. That's... a lot of major stereotypes about East Asian men, and he's <i>not</i> East Asian, but it still feels like a negative portrayal. The one dark-skinned character is addicted to drugs and also... you know, the villain of the fucking book. And the one other mixed-race character is a poor person who turns to thievery. Of the rich characters, two out of three are white, while <i>both</i> poor characters are not white. You can actually list the characters by wealth and the two wealthiest characters are white. If this connection were analyzed, it could be an interesting thematic element and parallel racism in real life. But it's not. And I recognize this could all be coincidence, but the fact that a <i>lot</i> of the characters here are racial stereotypes is pretty... uncomfortable. <br /><br />♚ The most genuinely upsetting part of this is that Avery, a "genetically perfect" model created by her parents, is blonde and white. Let's just emphasize this. <b>
  <u>She's genetically perfect because she's white. Genetic perfection = whiteness.</u>
</b> Yes, I recognize that this is the standard of beauty we know right now in America and Europe. Yes, I recognize that a lot of white authors haven't necessarily interrogated that. Yes, I recognize that this is probably an accident. But this is <b>straight-up racist eugenics</b>. In this supposedly racially diverse future world, making genetic manipulation <i>with the specific intent of beauty</i> lead to a white lead is genuinely horrifying. And on a related note, Avery is a far more terrible human being than most of the characters, yet she's given a lot of narrative sympathy other characters do not. <br /><br />(Arguably, any genetic manipulation is in and of itself eugenics, and I think any narrative wanting to talk about genetics should actually unpack that. But also, in 2016, I think unpacking felt like too much to ask from ya lit or lit in general to be fucking honest. So I'll just leave it at the bare-minimum standard of 'your genetic perfection being a white person has uncomfortable implications' and go. <br /><br />♚ This is a <b>
  <u>major, major spoiler</u>
</b> for the end and for book two, but it's also something I think sapphics especially will want to know before picking up: bury your gays. Severe. Because as we all know, burying BOTH of your queer lead characters for the development of your all-straight, all-alive cast is so <i>creative</i>. So <a href="https://glaad.org/files/WWAT/WWAT_GLAAD_2016-2017.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">never-before-done</a>. So <a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com/2018/02/04/please-stop-killing-me-lets-talk-about-buryyourgays/" rel="nofollow noopener">seldom-discussed</a>. Anyway, point is, if you write a book with, oh, maybe seven straight main characters, and then two sapphics, and you choose to bury the bi girl in your first book and the lesbian in your second book and all the straight people are still alive? <b>
  <u>Your book has a fucking problem.</u>
</b> <br /><br />VERDICT: I genuinely think this book is terrible. <b>I really would like to imagine this was all intentional, and the author will subvert it all in book three, but I really don't think that's at all what's happening here.</b> I'm tired and I'm angry and I am really done caring if people know it. I don't think this is a book or author that I want to support, ever.<br /><br /><a href="http://ellexamines.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/ellexamines" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5849796836751334181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1763185091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763185091" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763185091?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763185091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3301376047547723492">Confession time: <b>I'm partial to the occasional trashy, chick-lit novel</b>. You know the ones I mean. Those meaningless dramas where everyone sleeps with everyone and everyone betrays everyone and you are not required to think too hard. So when people were calling this a "futuristic <i>Gossip Girl</i>", that honestly didn't bother me. GG is an old guilty pleasure. Also, Chuck + Blair 4ever.<br/><br/>That's not the problem with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24921954.The_Thousandth_Floor__The_Thousandth_Floor___1_' title='The Thousandth Floor (The Thousandth Floor, #1) by Katharine McGee' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thousandth Floor</a>. <i>This</i> is the problem:<br/><blockquote>
  <i>On the other end of the call was Atlas, her b</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3301376047547723492" style="display:none">Confession time: <b>I'm partial to the occasional trashy, chick-lit novel</b>. You know the ones I mean. Those meaningless dramas where everyone sleeps with everyone and everyone betrays everyone and you are not required to think too hard. So when people were calling this a "futuristic <i>Gossip Girl</i>", that honestly didn't bother me. GG is an old guilty pleasure. Also, Chuck + Blair 4ever.<br /><br />That's not the problem with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24921954.The_Thousandth_Floor__The_Thousandth_Floor___1_" title="The Thousandth Floor (The Thousandth Floor, #1) by Katharine McGee" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thousandth Floor</a>. <i>This</i> is the problem:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>On the other end of the call was Atlas, her brother - and the reason she never wanted to kiss anyone else.</i>
</blockquote><br />Ick.<br /><br />I don't care that he's technically her step-brother; my issue with incest extends way beyond genetic factors. I don't mind when it appears to show abuse or is portrayed negatively, but I got the distinct impression that it's actually supposed to be sexy in this book. And I'm sorry, but I don't buy into the "consenting adults" argument for incest, or the comparisons with homosexuality. As <a href="http://www.slate.com/articles/health_and_science/human_nature/2010/12/incest_is_cancer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Saletan's Slate article says</a>:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Homosexuality is an orientation. Incest isn't. If the law bans gay sex, a lesbian can't have a sex life. But if you're hot for your sister, and the law says you can't sleep with her, you have billions of other options. Get out of your house, for God's sake. You'll find somebody to love without incinerating your family.</i>
</blockquote><br />It was a huge issue for me in a novel that could have easily been some mindless entertainment. McGee considers many different aspects of what the year 2118 might look like, from technology to global warming to designer babies. On top of that, it's a diverse book, as well as just a very interesting and rather... <i>dazzling</i> idea. Imagine a future where Manhattan literally becomes a vertical city in an enormous skyscraper; the extremely wealthy partying and getting high on the top floors.<br /><br /><b>But I just don't want to read about siblings making out</b>. I read to the end to find out who falls from the tower in the prologue, but I seriously considered not finishing it the moment Avery and Atlas lock lips. There are a lot of characters in this novel, all being young, stupid and scandalous, and I honestly quite enjoyed reading about their superficial lives, but I won't be returning for the sequel. That kind of "romance" is just not my thing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3301376047547723492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14258891160366878003" style="display:none">3.5* (maybe even closer to a 4, so I guess 3.75*)<br />This was a really fun, but also kind of sad, scifi read! <div id="review_1744901705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1744901705" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1744901705?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062564801" href="/book/show/29100329-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=poc">poc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=lgbtqi">lgbtqi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=packaged-book">packaged-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1744901705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8068237583732782362">THE THOUSANDTH FLOOR is <b>a sleek, smart, guilty pleasure</b>. The opening chapter begins with an unnamed girl falling to her death from a skyscraper in 22nd century New York, and the questions of "who" and "why" are ever-present as this thriller unfolds. The major raised eyebrow comes from the main character's love for her adopted brother, which sits rather uncomfortably for YA and in this context; but despite a few reservations, this story is surprisingly well-written and enjoyable. <br/><br/><b>Positives: </b><br/><br/>-- su</span>
  <span id="freeText8068237583732782362" style="display:none">THE THOUSANDTH FLOOR is <b>a sleek, smart, guilty pleasure</b>. The opening chapter begins with an unnamed girl falling to her death from a skyscraper in 22nd century New York, and the questions of "who" and "why" are ever-present as this thriller unfolds. The major raised eyebrow comes from the main character's love for her adopted brother, which sits rather uncomfortably for YA and in this context; but despite a few reservations, this story is surprisingly well-written and enjoyable. <br /><br /><b>Positives: </b><br /><br />-- super, <b>super fun world-building</b>. This is a mystery/thriller in a futuristic setting, with cool tech that feels organic to the story and the way the characters would use them. In addition to stuff you might expect, such as smart contacts with Google-glasses-type capabilities, there are imaginative touches like gummy bears with nano chips installed that make them move (and scream!), floating alcohol bubbles you drink from a straw, enviable closets and immersive shopping experiences, a boy with a frighteningly intuitive computer linked to his brain, and so much more. It's all incredibly well-thought-out, and none of it is there purely as set decoration.<br /><br />-- 5 distinct POVs, each of which add significantly to the plot. I'm the first person to complain about excessive and superfluous narrators, but you truly couldn't have lost one of these without changing the story. They're all well done, and all make you understand and sympathize with the characters' motivations, even when they're at odds with each other. One of the POVs is a teenage hacker's, and the description of how he infiltrates systems and uses information to his advantage is fascinating. <br /><br />-- realistic, layered friendships, especially between the girls. Affection, history, competition, and jealousy all come into play.<br /><br />-- There are major underlying <b>themes exploring class division and privilege</b> that I didn't expect. The towering, 1000-floor Manhattan building these kids live in is almost its own character, and the author skillfully and convincingly portrays the glittering lifestyle and mindset of the wealthy uptower kids and contrasting POVs without turning them all into cliches, or hammering readers with specific agendas and lessons. <br /><br />-- this future world is matter-of-factly <b>diverse</b>, with many persons of color, as well as LGBTQ characters. <br /><br />-- Sex-positive <br /><br />-- adults take a back seat here and maybe could have been developed a bit more, but they're not merely token presences; there are interesting subplots that happen with them. <br /><br /><b>Stuff I wish had been better:</b><br /><br />-- Avery is in love with her adopted brother. It's not handled in an icky way, but <b>romanticizing incest</b> for young readers is something that does concern me, particularly when it involves kids who were mostly raised and grew up together. It's less of an issue for me in other situations--dire ones like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7600924.Forbidden" title="Forbidden by Tabitha Suzuma" rel="nofollow noopener">Forbidden</a> come to mind--but here, the single-mindedness and focus on this romance would make me less inclined to recommend this for younger teenagers, especially since the connection between the two of them isn't as well-developed as it could be. Atlas is kind of a pleasant but oblique non-entity; Avery, despite her genetic perfection, is much more interesting. <br /><br />-- I really, really wish <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the girl who is killed isn't the bisexual one. With all the "kill your gays" issues of late,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I think <b>increased mindfulness and sensitivity to this trope is necessary</b>. <br /><br />-- I'm not sure this needed a sequel, since I think the story would have more of an impact if it had stuck the ending. But I enjoyed this so much, I'll definitely be picking up book two!<br /><br />This was longer than I intended, but since there are so many mixed/negative reviews I thought a countering opinion might be useful. Despite a couple of not-insignificant issues, I think this one has a lot going for it, and I liked that it wasn't a typical fast-paced, action-heavy thriller, but more of a character-driven story with a futuristic setting. I was completely engrossed as I went down all the rabbit holes of the plot, and the future tech is so freaking cool. Damn, it's fun to live and play in this world, even if it's just for a little while.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8068237583732782362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9626022585464520507">i love my YA books like i love drama - wild, reckless, and over-the-top. and the thousandth floor was all of that and more! i couldnt get enough. seriously, this book/series is soooo underrated and its a tragedy.<br/><br/>now, dont get me wrong. this wont win any literary awards or become a classic anytime soon (if at all). the writing is relatively simplistic and the overall tone feels young, but that totally works for this type of story. its serving me drama, dangerous flirtations, over-privileged kids </span>
  <span id="freeText9626022585464520507" style="display:none">i love my YA books like i love drama - wild, reckless, and over-the-top. and the thousandth floor was all of that and more! i couldnt get enough. seriously, this book/series is soooo underrated and its a tragedy.<br /><br />now, dont get me wrong. this wont win any literary awards or become a classic anytime soon (if at all). the writing is relatively simplistic and the overall tone feels young, but that totally works for this type of story. its serving me drama, dangerous flirtations, over-privileged kids who dont think before they act. its a recipe for disaster and i am here for it. <br /><br />this has been compared to ‘gossip girl,’ and although i can see the similarities, this was such an entertaining story in its own right. its so unique with its sci-fi-esque world building, it has great character arcs, and dont forget all the DRAMA. it is the very definition of a guilty pleasure series but, somehow, i dont feel too guilty about enjoying it.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1230810208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230810208" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230810208?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230810208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7907389761603670635"><blockquote>
  <i>all he knew was that the girl was the first person to fall from the Tower in its twenty-five years. He didn't know who she was, or how she'd gotten outside.<br/>He didn't know whether she'd fallen, or been pushed, or whether - crushed by the weight of unspoken secrets - she'd decided to jump.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I know the book comparisons get old, but think futuristic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_' title='Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar' rel='nofollow noopener'> Gossip Girl</a>. I was pleased with how excellent the drama was. Definitely one of those guilty pleasure type books. What elevated things for me was the </span>
  <span id="freeText7907389761603670635" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>all he knew was that the girl was the first person to fall from the Tower in its twenty-five years. He didn't know who she was, or how she'd gotten outside.<br />He didn't know whether she'd fallen, or been pushed, or whether - crushed by the weight of unspoken secrets - she'd decided to jump.</i>
</blockquote><br />I know the book comparisons get old, but think futuristic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gossip Girl</a>. I was pleased with how excellent the drama was. Definitely one of those guilty pleasure type books. What elevated things for me was the incredible world that was created. Set in New York City in the year 2118 - a world like you've never seen before! The city is a thousand-story tower stretching two and a half miles high.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Leda caught flashes of color where the elevators shot past, the veins of the city pumping its lifeblood up and down. It was the same as ever, she thought, utterly modern and and yet somehow timeless. Leda had seen countless pics of the old New York skyline, the one people always romanticized. But compared to the tower she thought it looked jagged and ugly.</i>
</blockquote><br />The higher up in the Tower you live, the wealthier you are. Also meaning the lower the floor, the poorer you are. This futuristic world is very high-tech with hovers as cars, retinal scans to unlock doors, contacts as a quicker means of a computer really with the capability of looking stuff up by saying it aloud, sending pings or texts, checking the feeds or social media, etc. The lower the level, the less futuristic tech you will find because they can't be afforded. There's futuristic drugs like halluci-lighters and really all kinds of things. This world is very expansive..<br /><br />The story starts with the inevitable end: a girl falling off the Tower from a party on the thousandth floor. We don't know who she is, how she got there, or how she ends up falling two and a half miles to her death.<br /><br />It backtracks two months and this is where we meet our characters. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24921954.The_Thousandth_Floor__The_Thousandth_Floor___1_" title="The Thousandth Floor (The Thousandth Floor, #1) by Katharine McGee" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Thousandth Floor</a> is told from five different perspectives.<br /><br />Avery is the girl who was genetically created to be perfect (a word she despises). She lives on the thousandth floor with her parents and brother Atlas. Her life should be <i>perfect</i>, right? Only she is tormented by the one thing she wants, but could never have.<br /><br />Leda is fresh off a stint in rehab, something she won't let anyone find out about for fear of being judged. She's even keeping it from her best friend Avery. It was only xenperheidren which helps to sharpen her thinking. It just felt so necessary until it all got out of control after what happened last year - that hookup with Atlas nobody knows about. And he left after, went missing. The only person he talks to is Avery, but no one knows where he is. Can Leda keep her secret addiction under control amidst the chaos the Tower brings her?<br /><br />Rylin lives on the thirty-second floor with her younger sister. Their mom died a year ago leaving Rylin to work a dead-end job and keep things afloat. She has a drug dealing boyfriend and is always behind on rent. So when an opportunity to work on one of the highest floors in the Tower comes her way, she couldn't possibly turn it down. If only she knew how much this job would truly cost her.<br /><br />Eris comes from old family money and is Avery's oldest friend. Upon new information, her life begins to fall apart at the seams. Her whole world flips upside down.<br /><br />Watt is a genius living on the 240th floor with his family. He has a deep secret that could get him locked up in prison for life. It's also the reason why he's so damn good at hacking. And why he gets hired by one of the upper-level girls to spy on someone making the lies go deeper than even he could imagine.<br /><br />There's a whole lot more to the plot, but I'd view some of these little things as spoilers. It's best to find out as you go along. Just know there's a whole lot more drama involved. There's a complicated and not-so-typical love triangle, financial issues, problems with parents and siblings, a secret addiction, and really so so much more. I even feel like there were some things alluded to, just not quite gotten to yet in the plot. I'm really excited to see where the series takes us from here. I enjoyed all of the characters. Some are more likable than others, but I found myself intrigued by all of the characters' individual stories. I loved the futuristic aspects within the story. I'd like to learn more about how things came to be the way they are, though. I wish there was a little bit more world-building to explain certain complexities. However there was just enough in book one. I only hope to see the world expanded a bit more.<br /><br />Prepare for plenty of backstabbing, secrets, betrayal, romance, and even more. Bonus for excellent diversity. And bisexual characters like it ain't no thang. Finally with it in the future. If you've enjoyed anything by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/93970.Sara_Shepard" title="Sara Shepard" rel="nofollow noopener"> Sara Shepard</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/381489.Private__Private___1_" title="Private (Private, #1) by Kate Brian" rel="nofollow noopener"> Private</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gossip Girl</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22999141.Emancipated__Emancipated___1_" title="Emancipated (Emancipated, #1) by M.G. Reyes" rel="nofollow noopener"> Emancipated</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26116460.Unrivaled__Beautiful_Idols___1_" title="Unrivaled (Beautiful Idols, #1) by Alyson Noel" rel="nofollow noopener"> Unrivaled</a>, or any series like these, you'll fall in love with the world Katharine McGee created.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7907389761603670635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1894119044" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894119044" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894119044?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062570130" href="/book/show/29505416-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Teen Drama fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894119044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15610767790642382939">4.5 starts rounded up to 5<br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised by this book. I kept seeing it in my feed, but it seemed like the reception has been a bit lukewarm. The concept sounded interesting so I figured I would give it a try.<br/><br/>You might look at this YA teen drama and say to yourself, “Matthew, this doesn’t seem like your type of book!” Well, I do like to dabble in the teen drama a bit – I blame my years of watching Degrassi for keeping a nostalgic corner of my heart for the genre. Also, my wife is alw</span>
  <span id="freeText15610767790642382939" style="display:none">4.5 starts rounded up to 5<br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised by this book. I kept seeing it in my feed, but it seemed like the reception has been a bit lukewarm. The concept sounded interesting so I figured I would give it a try.<br /><br />You might look at this YA teen drama and say to yourself, “Matthew, this doesn’t seem like your type of book!” Well, I do like to dabble in the teen drama a bit – I blame my years of watching Degrassi for keeping a nostalgic corner of my heart for the genre. Also, my wife is always watching Pretty Little Liars, Vampire Diaries, etc. – which I find myself watching along with her. So, I have to say this sort of thing is my not-so-guilty pleasure!<br /><br />I thought the storytelling and characters were great. For me it felt a lot like the Lunar Chronicles in its format, but I may have actually liked how this one started a bit more (and I really liked Cinder). When I first got into it and realized that it was going to be pretty heavy on the teenage angst and rumor mongering, I worried that it would descend into a simple pattern of backstabbing and gossiping. But, I think it stayed fairly interesting and complex. She built the plot in such a way that when you get to the resolution you realize almost every single plot point helped to weave an intricate web. Very cool!<br /><br />My only possible complaint is that it overdid the "oops-I-wasn't-supposed-to-see-that-but-now-I-am-going-to-misinterpret-what-I-saw" trope. I think it happened at least 5 times and there has to be a max quota of this for one book!<br /><br />Side Note: I noticed that the follow-up books in this trilogy were better received and rated. This has led me to a theory – I will officially dub it “Matthew’s Trilogy Rating Theory” and get it trademarked! ;) I often notice that the next two books in a trilogy tend to rate better than the first. Normally my thought would be that the story got better or the author got more comfortable writing scenarios for their characters. Now I am thinking it is more that, on average, if you didn’t like the first, you are much less likely to keep going. Therefore, a greater percentage of the reviewers of the next two books are people who loved the first and are, therefore more likely to rate the sequels high as well. I am sure there is a complex mathematical equation for this around here somewhere . . .<br /><br />My conclusion – I do recommend the book, but since many are rating it mediocre, I cannot say for sure if you will be as pumped about it as I was. But, if you do end up liking it, I think you will REALLY like it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15610767790642382939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2187593145?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" href="/user/show/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog">Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2187593145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5014904705272489067">The Thousandth Floor is a YA novel set in the future. All the characters in the book live in a giant tower located in New York city. The amount of wealth and status citizens possess dictates where they live in the tower. The wealthiest families live on the top floors, the poorest on the bottom, and everyone else in between. <br/><br/>Throughout the story, we follow 5 characters, Avery, Eris, Watt, Rylin, and Leda, and get to read from each of their points of view. The book is written in third person. That</span>
  <span id="freeText5014904705272489067" style="display:none">The Thousandth Floor is a YA novel set in the future. All the characters in the book live in a giant tower located in New York city. The amount of wealth and status citizens possess dictates where they live in the tower. The wealthiest families live on the top floors, the poorest on the bottom, and everyone else in between. <br /><br />Throughout the story, we follow 5 characters, Avery, Eris, Watt, Rylin, and Leda, and get to read from each of their points of view. The book is written in third person. That's not my favorite, but I think it worked well here. It took me a little while to get into the story, but that was mostly because I was switching back and forth between 5 different people. It was absolutely necessary though to set up the story, and after a certain point, I was hooked! <br /><br />Secrets and lies are at the root of most of the characters troubles. Whether it be keeping them or telling them, no one is immune from the damage they cause. One of them even winds up dead, and finding out who falls from the top of the tower propelled me to plow through the second half of the book. The author did an amazing job of creating suspense in the last few chapters. I couldn't put the book down if I had to!<br /><br />The ending is unforgettable and infuriating! Never has a book ending made me so absolutely livid! I was literally yelling at my kindle like a crazy person. I'm serious. People were staring! It wasn't pretty! Lol I couldn't even rate the book when I was done, because I was so furious! <br /><br />After I slept on it, I realized that the fact that I felt so passionately about the end and that I cared so much for the character that wound up on the ground means that the author did a damn good job with making me invested. I felt so much for the character that met their demise. I wanted to scream! I wanted to cry! I wanted to write to Katherine and tell her that she broke my heart! I would also tell her that she is fucking amazing at the same time. <br /><br />I've seen many mixed reviews for this book, and most of them seem to be due to the ending. I understand why, because it isn't a happy one by any means. We still have two more books to go though, and I'm holding out hope that I'm satisfied in the end! It won't change what happened, but hopefully, it makes me feel better in some way. It's driving me crazy not to grab the second book right away to see what happens next. I'm reading these with my book club though, so suffer I shall until we have the next one scheduled. I recommend this book with the warning that it will drive you crazy and piss you off beyond belief! In my case, it was worth it. Your mileage may vary!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5014904705272489067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16125620179545582504"><b>You might like this if:</b><br/>-You liked Pretty Little Liars or anything else by Sara Shepard (or Gossip Girl according to every other review, but I never saw or read that one to compare). <br/>-You like stories that hinge on lies, frenemies, and revenge.<br/>-You like books with enough POVs that even when you really hate one character/situation, there are plenty of others to get invested in to balance it out.<br/><br/><b>You might not like this if:</b><br/>-You dislike stories about privileged rich kids doing drugs upon drugs out of</span>
  <span id="freeText16125620179545582504" style="display:none"><b>You might like this if:</b><br />-You liked Pretty Little Liars or anything else by Sara Shepard (or Gossip Girl according to every other review, but I never saw or read that one to compare). <br />-You like stories that hinge on lies, frenemies, and revenge.<br />-You like books with enough POVs that even when you really hate one character/situation, there are plenty of others to get invested in to balance it out.<br /><br /><b>You might not like this if:</b><br />-You dislike stories about privileged rich kids doing drugs upon drugs out of boredom.<br />-You're skeeved out that one of the characters has a crush on their adopted sibling that they grew up with. It's a major storyline in the book.<br /><br />Diversity: Leda is black. Watt is Iranian. Eris is bi. I may have missed other identifiers.<br /><br />It took me about halfway in to get into this because I was so grossed out by the sibling crush, but then I got invested in the other characters. I did like how the book opens with someone falling to their death and you don't know who it is or if they were pushed or jumped, and the story goes back a few months and you read everything leading up to that wondering who it will be and why.<br /><br />Basically, this book is exactly what it says it is. Lies, drama, parties.</span>

<div id="review_1737321575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1737321575" />
    <a title="Cila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27011842-cila"><img alt="Cila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547850070p2/27011842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1737321575?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cila" href="/user/show/27011842-cila">Cila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1737321575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7517298858052069927"><b>
  <i>“Up here on the roof, so close to the stars, she felt young and alive and hateful.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Hateful is a little harsh but annoying certainly fits the bill; it’s very hard for me to finish a book and not find a single character likable but alas, here we have it. Still, there were a couple of elements that made me like this book, and tons that didn't. If you like gossipy high school-ish petty drama this book might be for you, but I'll leave it up to you dear reader whether or not to embark on a 400+ pa</span>
  <span id="freeText7517298858052069927" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Up here on the roof, so close to the stars, she felt young and alive and hateful.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Hateful is a little harsh but annoying certainly fits the bill; it’s very hard for me to finish a book and not find a single character likable but alas, here we have it. Still, there were a couple of elements that made me like this book, and tons that didn't. If you like gossipy high school-ish petty drama this book might be for you, but I'll leave it up to you dear reader whether or not to embark on a 400+ page ride that leads to nowhere. So here are the Pro’s and Con’s.<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />• The cover, packaging and art of this book. It's amazingly <i>gorgeous</i> in person, seriously one of the prettiest I've seen, looks great in any library. <br /><br />• The technology described in the book doesn’t sound far-fetched and maybe actually achievable in the future; I loved it when she talked about the gadgets they all used, and kept thinking to myself <i>“Damn I wish those were around now.”</i> (The hologram that enables you to try on outfits without having to move a single muscle was my particular favorite).<br /><br />• The tower concept is also very cool and not something I’ve read about before, I loved the fact that it had absolutely everything in it, from aquariums to pieces of Central Park. <br /><br />• The idea that a ride to Paris, France is only three hours away by undersea transportation.<br /><br />• This fact that this book is <u>NOT</u> dystopian as some would have you think, it’s the future yes, but nothing like other YA novels portray it; the only problem seemed to be global warming, (which let’s face it we’re already suffering the effects of now), apart from that everything is just modernized and a reality I could definitely see myself living in. <br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />• The characters, not a *single* salvageable one - except maybe Maribel (but this remains to be seen in the next book because she has very little scenes in this one); I hated them all a little and for different reasons, but at the end of the day they were all <i>100% <b>SHALLOW.</b></i> Although I did have a particular hate for Leda, <b>DIE LEDA DIE!</b> <br /><br />• I guarantee the only reason you’ll keep reading till the end is to find out who the hell ended up being scraped off the pavement after falling from the thousandth floor. (Which is actually the prologue of this book so no spoilers there). Which leads me to the next thing...<br /><br />• The cliffhanger, yes you heard me, after 400+ pages, the plot is left half-way and if you want to find out what happens, I’m guessing we’ll have to purchase the <u>next book.</u><br /><br />• Last but certainly not least - the incest. One of the characters is completely obsessed with her brother, and whilst he is her <i>half-brother</i>, they still grew up together and let’s all face it, that’s f-ing weird. Maybe it’s because I’m a sibling myself but I strongly believe in the nurture vs. nature, if you raise someone to be your brother/son/daughter then that is your family, <b>period.</b> <br /><br />So in total I give this book 3 stars and will begrudgingly buy the next one - but only if the cover is as <i>sexy</i> as the first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7517298858052069927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1648425546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648425546" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648425546?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-read">r2r-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648425546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3966165048523952002">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Was she ready for this – ready to come back here and face everything that had sent her into a tailspin in the first place?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516156.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a YA futuristic story, about a group of teenagers living in a thousand-floor tower in New York City. <br/><br/>Avery was a girl who lived at the top of the tower, and had a crush on the one person she couldn’t possibly be with – her adopted b</span>
  <span id="freeText3966165048523952002" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Was she ready for this – ready to come back here and face everything that had sent her into a tailspin in the first place?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516156.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a YA futuristic story, about a group of teenagers living in a thousand-floor tower in New York City. <br><br>Avery was a girl who lived at the top of the tower, and had a crush on the one person she couldn’t possibly be with – her adopted brother Atlas. We then got a bit of a weird love-triangle going on, with Avery, Atlas, and Avery’s best friend Leda, with Avery hopelessly hung up on Atlas and having no clue what to do about it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“On the other end of the call was Atlas, her brother – and the reason she never wanted to kiss anyone else.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450211572i/17393530._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Leda, Avery’s best friend, had just gotten out of a stint in rehab after getting hooked on a prescription-only medication which aided concentration (xenperheidren). She had previously slept with Atlas, and was intent on repeating the experience, to the extent that she hired a hacker to track his every move and feed her back information.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She didn’t need the drugs, not the way those girls did.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516157._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eris, Avery’s other best friend, also lived near the top of the tower, and very quickly found out that he father wasn’t her biological father, and ended up moving to a much lower level apartment with her mother. We then got a surprise about who her biological father really was, which shook things up a bit, and we also got a romantic storyline involving Eris and a girl who lived near her new apartment. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Her mom had cheated on her dad, and kept it a secret for the past eighteen years.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516158.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rylin lived with her sister on one of the lower floors following the death of her mother. She had a boyfriend who dealt drugs, and a dead-end job, and we got a storyline involving the drugs, and a boy called Cord who lived on one of the upper floors. I was actually quite surprised that we didn’t get a storyline from Cord’s point of view as he seemed like quite a major character.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Two hundred nanodollars for just one night dealing with drunk rich kids? “How soon do you need me there?””</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516159.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Watt was a hacker who basically had an AI type thing in his head which was totally illegal, was hired by Leda to try and track Atlas, and developed a bit of a crush on Avery, which was pretty hopeless because of the whole Avery-Atlas-Leda love triangle. His hacking skills were pretty impressive though.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was in possession of an illegal quant, and he needed to hide her somewhere she could never be found.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466760894i/19516160._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was woven together by the characters interlocking stories, and it seemed like everyone had something to hide. The pace was a little bit slow, but I think this was probably necessary because of how many main characters there were, and the way their stories all coincided. <br><br>The ending to this was quite shocking, as someone died, and someone else started blackmailing people to cover up their part in the murder! Will be interesting to see what happens in the next book!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066772i/15045457.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>7 out of 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="3966165048523952002" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1981642390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981642390" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981642390?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=dystopian-and-scifi">dystopian-and-scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=psy-thriller-crime">psy-thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=ya-na-contemporaries">ya-na-contemporaries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981642390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9555440835139749445"><blockquote>
  <i>They say that before death, people’s lives flash before their eyes. But as the ground rushed ever faster toward her, the girl could think only of the past few hours, the path she’d taken that ended here. If only she hadn’t talked to him. If only she hadn’t been so foolish. If only she hadn’t gone up there in the first place.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>THIS BOOK IS A FREAKING TREAT!<br/><br/>When I first added it to my tbr, months ago, I would have never imagined it to suck me in the way it did. I basically devoured it and with e</span>
  <span id="freeText9555440835139749445" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>They say that before death, people’s lives flash before their eyes. But as the ground rushed ever faster toward her, the girl could think only of the past few hours, the path she’d taken that ended here. If only she hadn’t talked to him. If only she hadn’t been so foolish. If only she hadn’t gone up there in the first place.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><br>THIS BOOK IS A FREAKING TREAT!<br><br>When I first added it to my tbr, months ago, I would have never imagined it to suck me in the way it did. I basically devoured it and with every turn of the page, I felt myself clinging onto the various subplots like my life depended on it.<br>It's nothing extraordinary or life-changing, but I had so much fun soaking in the drama Avery, Leda, Eris and Rylin were experiencing I think I might need to continue the series. <br>Also, when I searched the tags and found out belongs to the dystopian category, I expected a world in ruins (because that's how Hunger Games &amp; Co. grew me), or a lot of world-building and politics (again, I'm blaming HG), but I didn't find any of this. <br>I don't really know if this pleases me or not, but, who cares???<br>Whether you read it for the plot, the characters, the drama, the romance, the whatever-you-want-to-call-it, just dive into this expecting nothing but entertainment, because entertainment is what you'll get. <br><a href="http://it.tinypic.com?ref=2ch7tjb" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540481662ra/26500697.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Lol, sorry, that was random, but I can't put into words how much fun I had while reading this. It kind of brought me back to a time where I was obsessed and in love with Serena Van Der Woodsen (and, consequently, Blake Lively) and I spent my afternoons binge-watching GG with my friends.<br><br><br>I have a few other complainings about it, to be completely honest, but they're a bit spoiler-y so I'll keep them so myself. They're not that important, anyway. *rubs hands* I loved it. What's more important than that?!<br><br><br>Sometimes all you need is to read a book that won't teach you a flipping beep but that's juicy interesting just the same. <br>Sometimes all you need is to read a book that allows you to act like a little spy into someone else's amazing (and totally fucked-up) life. <br>Sometimes all you need is to read a book packed with intrigues, teen drama, futuristic technology and Gossip Girl-like scenarios. <br>Sometimes, all you need is a Katharine McGee book. <br>And, damn, only the bookish goddess herself knows how, for me, this was without a doubt one of those times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9555440835139749445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
