<div id="review_1996532119" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996532119" />
    <a title="Kimberly (Deity of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books"><img alt="Kimberly (Deity of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600646134p2/65929813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996532119?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly (Deity of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly (Deity of Books)" href="/user/show/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books">Kimberly (Deity of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062418593" href="/book/show/28218953-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books?shelf=helpful-reviews">helpful-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65929813-kimberly-deity-of-books?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996532119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6899191470788593784"><b>This is a trashy, fun read filled with dramatic romance and stupid teenagers, but I still like it, given that I've read it 4 times and even annotated it.</b><br/><br/>The book opens with an unknown girl falling off the thousandth floor of The Tower, a thousand-floor skyscraper in Manhattan, 2118.<br/><br/>Then it goes back to two months before the incident, where we meet <b>Avery</b>, who lives on the thousandth floor. She is the perfect girl—literally. Her parents picked out the best genes from their gene pools and made her.</span>
  <span id="freeText6899191470788593784" style="display:none"><b>This is a trashy, fun read filled with dramatic romance and stupid teenagers, but I still like it, given that I've read it 4 times and even annotated it.</b><br /><br />The book opens with an unknown girl falling off the thousandth floor of The Tower, a thousand-floor skyscraper in Manhattan, 2118.<br /><br />Then it goes back to two months before the incident, where we meet <b>Avery</b>, who lives on the thousandth floor. She is the perfect girl—literally. Her parents picked out the best genes from their gene pools and made her. She's a "custom made baby". She is like that girl that you want to hate, but can’t. Atlas is her adoptive brother and she is in love with him.<br /><br />The next person we meet is <b>Leda</b>. She lives on the 962nd floor and is a recovering drug addict, who just got out of rehab. No one, but her family knows this—not even her best friend, Avery. Why? Well, Leda and Avery have been drifting apart. They used to tell each other everything, but now they are both keeping something from each other. Avery is obviously hiding the fact that she is in love with Atlas and Leda… she's hiding the fact that she hooked up with Atlas during winter vacation. <br /><br /><i>**sniff, sniff**</i><br />Do you smell that?<br />It's a love triangle brewing.<br /><br /><b>Rylin</b> lives on the 32nd floor. She is an orphan and has a younger sister named Chrissa. She works hard every day to ensure her sister lives well and can go to college. One day, she is out partying with her friends and her boyfriend when she receives a call from Cord Anderton. He is around Rylin's age and an orphan as well. He's loaded and lives on the 969th floor. Rylin's mother used to be a maid for them. Rylin receives this call from Cord because he's hosting a party and needs a maid.<br /><br /><b>Eris</b> lives on the 985th floor and is one of Avery’s best friends. She’s a playgirl. She comes from old money. Eris and her parents have a great relationship until a shocking truth is revealed.<br /><br /><b>Watt</b> lives on the 294th floor. He is a tech genius that built his own illegal quantum computer named Nadia. She, Nadia, is embedded in Watt’s brain and helps him get girls, good grades, and money. His family is tight on money, so Watt and Nadia team up to take hacking jobs.<br /><br /><i>So how do all these characters get entwined with each other? You’ll have to read to find out.</i><br /><br />The beginning of the book is probably one of the best hooks I’ve ever read. I normally don't like high school drama or romance books, but this book is different. This is a thriller and it’s probably the first I’ve read. I’ll definitely be reading more thrillers. The characters have a lot of depth and are very interesting despite the questionable and morally wrong decisions they make. <br /><br />The characters in this book are very easily distinguishable even though there are 5 POVs (Avery, Leda, Rylin, Eris, and Watt) because it’s written in third person and the characters all have different voices (or maybe it's just because I've read this book 4 times already).<br /><br />The levels of The Tower symbolize wealth. The higher a person lives in The Tower means that the more wealth a person has. I love that the author showed all levels of society in this world. The majority of the book takes place in The Tower. There are restaurants, bars, spas, parks, farms, supermarkets, shops, etc… in The Tower. <br /><br />You won’t find out who the girl that fell from the Tower is until the end. It’s like a murder mystery. It might seem super boring to read through 400 pages and only at the end find out who the girl is. But it’s not. All the 400 pages in between are super entertaining. <br /><br /><b>You will hate all the characters at some point</b>. In some chapters, I love them, and in others, I hate them and am so annoyed with the choices they made. <br /><br />The character that I disliked the most was Leda. I hated that she always compared herself to others to make herself better and that she looked down on people with less wealth than her. She is smart in some aspects, but definitely not when it’s love. <br /><br />The thing that bugged me the most was the incest. It’s not a spoiler because it was revealed in the first couple of characters. It’s between Avery and her brother, Atlas. Atlas is her adoptive brother, but still. It’s annoying and disgusting. I got so sick of this “romance”. I kept skipping over pages of Avery and Atlas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6899191470788593784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1741246082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1741246082" />
    <a title="Lia  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48295288-lia"><img alt="Lia  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594824825p2/48295288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1741246082?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia  " href="/user/show/48295288-lia">Lia  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=english-and-american-lit-and-more">english-and-american-lit-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=junk-food-for-my-brain">junk-food-for-my-brain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1741246082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15720978900008132393"><b>
  <u>3.5 stars</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>This book was such a <i>lovely</i> guilty pleasure. Like treating yourself to a lazy reading day even though you have a lot of work to do; you know you shouldn't, but you don't really care, and you enjoy every second of it. <br/>If you've read a couple of reviews on this book already, you've probably already heard what everyone else is saying - that this book is basically a futuristic version of Gossip Girl and Pretty Little Liars. Which is true, to some extent. I don't normally enjoy reading b</span>
  <span id="freeText15720978900008132393" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>3.5 stars</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><br />This book was such a <i>lovely</i> guilty pleasure. Like treating yourself to a lazy reading day even though you have a lot of work to do; you know you shouldn't, but you don't really care, and you enjoy every second of it. <br />If you've read a couple of reviews on this book already, you've probably already heard what everyone else is saying - that this book is basically a futuristic version of Gossip Girl and Pretty Little Liars. Which is true, to some extent. I don't normally enjoy reading books about petty rich people problems. Boo-hoo, you got a wine stain on your new Chanel dress. Poor you, you're so beautiful that people only approach you because of your looks! But sometimes, to get away from Real Life Problems, this is exactly what I need to read. And, somehow, this book managed to never annoy me, even though most of the characters (but not all of them) were definitely too spoiled for their own good. <br /><br />The Thousandth Floor is set in <u>New York City, one hundred years from now.</u> All the major cities in the world now have a one thousandth stories Tower, which is basically like a city inside a city. The richer you are, the higher your floor is. They live in a highly technological world, and can do almost anything they want in a matter of seconds. Everything is faster and more comfortable, as long as you're rich enough to afford it. <br /><br /><b>Rylin</b> lives on the 32nd floor with her younger sister. After their mum passed away, Rylin was forced to drop out of school and to get a job - or several - in order to pay rent and send her sister to school. She can't help but look with utter disdain at the people who live on the highest floors. Until one day, broke and desperate, she has to make a difficult choice.<br /><br /><b>Eris</b> is pretty, bubbly and carefree. Her parents love her, and have spoiled her her whole life. She always smiles, goes to all the parties, hooks up with all the beautiful boys and girls. And then, suddenly, her perfect life shatters completely, and she is forced to face reality. <br /><br /><b>Leda</b> has never felt like she's good enough. She is rich, pretty but severe-looking, and she's hiding one too many secrets. Something happened one night, that she can't tell anyone about. People keep asking her where she's been all summer, and Leda keeps lying to them, but all those lies are starting to weigh on her heart, and her mind is becoming a darker and darker place... <br /><br /><b>Watt</b> is a hacker. He's a bit too smart and a bit too resourceful, and he knows that what he does can be very dangerous. He bends the rules - the law - in an almost careless way. He knows everything about everyone, and nothing ever feels new to him, not when he has some <i>extra help</i> that allows him not to ever make a misstep. <br /><br /><b>Avery</b> is the most beautiful girl on earth - genetically engineered by her parents to be so. She lives on the thousandth floor, and people think she's untouchable. She used to be best friends with Leda, but now they are slowly drifting apart. But Avery, seemingly perfect and detached from the entire world, is hiding a dark secret that no one can know about. She is in love with someone she can <i>never</i> have. <br /><br />The book is told from <u>five different points of view</u>, and though their voices weren't all that different from one another, each character had their own unique perspective on things. Their stories slowly started to collide, becoming tangled and more and more complicated. It was a bit Gossip Girl-like in the way that everyone was sleeping with everyone and even the most innocent people were hiding unspeakable secrets, but I enjoyed most of the characters and their arcs nonetheless. It was also interesting to have a good amount of diversity, both in terms of ethnicity and sexual orientation, and while most of the focus was on a privileged world of wealthy - but not so happy - people, we also got to see the struggles of the lower classes. The writing was better than I expected, which made the book extremely easy to read, and some of the characters surprised me in their complexity. If some of them felt a bit shallow, as if the author had just started to shape their personality (just to mention a few: Eris, Cord, Watt...), some of them turned out to be quite disconcerting (mostly Leda, who was much more twisted than I had originally anticipated.) While none of the romantic pairings were particularly swoon-worthy - though I think I would've liked Cord if he had been a bit more developed - they were all interesting enough. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The "love triangle" between Leda, her best friend Avery and Avery's adoptive brother, Atlas, was unexpected, dark and weirdly fascinating. The only thing that annoyed me quite a bit was that, in the end, the person that fell off the tower - or, should I say, was pushed by Leda - was Eris. Not only she probably was the most "innocent" of them all, but she was also our only LGBTQIA+ main character. And she died. I wish authors would stop doing this all the time, and realise that it's also possible to let your queer characters live, and that you don't necessarily have to kill them off at the first chance you get. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />Since I was mostly entertained by all the drama, the biggest problem I had with The Thousandth Floor was probably the absolute lack of world-building. Look, I'm a Linguistics major. I'm not exactly a mechanical engineer. But even <i>I</i> could tell that the technology displayed in the book was a bit too far-fetched, especially since no explanation was ever provided for it. I'm not saying that I wanted entire pages explaining how all the machinery worked because, no thanks, but it would have been nice if the author had at least hinted to the new technological discoveries, or to why the Towers even existed in the first place. And what about the genetic engineering for unborn children? Still, I cannot deny that I had a lot of fun reading this book, and I am rather impatient for the second installment to come out (I'm not yet sure if this is a trilogy or a duology, but after that ending, I really want to know how the situation will evolve.) <br /><br /><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Sometimes, love and chaos are the same thing."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15720978900008132393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1767277906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767277906" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767277906?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008179977" href="/book/show/31244354-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=harper-collins-australia">harper-collins-australia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767277906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16036143219305528156">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2016/10/21/thousandth-floor-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>So it appears that you can disagree with your co-bloggers on books. While Jenna loved The Thousandth Floor, I could not stand it.<br/><br/>It started out promising, with the use of technological advancements leading to life with Manhattan in a thousand floor tower. Those who live at the top, such as Avery and her friends, live a charmed life filled with parties, drugs, gossip and opulence, while those who live towards the bottom live </span>
  <span id="freeText16036143219305528156" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2016/10/21/thousandth-floor-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />So it appears that you can disagree with your co-bloggers on books. While Jenna loved The Thousandth Floor, I could not stand it.<br /><br />It started out promising, with the use of technological advancements leading to life with Manhattan in a thousand floor tower. Those who live at the top, such as Avery and her friends, live a charmed life filled with parties, drugs, gossip and opulence, while those who live towards the bottom live a life of poverty. I found the use of technology throughout the novel to be really fascinating, especially when contrasted to the lives of the poorer Rylin who has to work as a cleaner and Eris who has to move to the lower levels.<br /><br />There’s some interesting concepts here, where everyone wears contacts which acts as super computers. They can watch TV from these contacts, read people’s lips, but the contacts are directed by voice commands. There’s also bars filled with hoverboards, dresses filled with illuminated mirrors and genetically modified flowers that attract light.<br /><br />The real reason I couldn’t stand The Thousandth Floor however, is also the same reason why I couldn’t continue with the Mortal Instruments series past the first few books – it contains a hefty dose of brother-sister romance, or incest. I don’t care if Avery and Atlas aren’t related by blood and they’re technically step-siblings, but hearing about them pining away for one another made me uncomfortable. And it’s not just a brief mention, in fact most of the book is centered around this and the drama and the fall out from it.<br /><br />I wasn’t particularly interested in any of the characters either, I felt like they got pretty boring really fast. While on the upside, their dramas and complaints seemed to be valid, it was filled with nonsensical friendship and romantic drama that doesn’t really go anywhere until the last few chapters of the book. Avery pines away for Atlas, Leda and Watt who start dating them wonder why they’re aloof, Eris starts dating someone from a lower floor and Rylin starts dating Cole. It all felt a bit too messy and convoluted and no one really interacted with each other outside of the parties outside of their thoughts.<br /><br />Watt was probably the most interesting character for me, who has a supercomputer Nadia embedded into his skull. But when he decided to use his skills for picking up Avery and hacking instead of anything particularly useful, he soon lost his appeal. He also felt a lot like Dan from Gossip Girl, the typical outsider who isn’t that attractive but somehow works his way into the in crowd. I didn’t like Dan at all, which also summarises my feelings on Watt.<br /><br />The heavy use of drugs and alcohol was also rather disturbing here, with Leda as a drug addict recovering from rehab and Rylin’s involvement with people who deal in drugs. Their use of hardcore drugs and partying rarely had any repercussions outside of a simple hangover. You would think for someone like Leda, that this would be handled with more care, but it felt like it was added for more dramatic effect. She used the drugs to cope with the drama but there wasn’t any guilt or much thought around the restraint behind this.<br /><br />Whether you’d be able to stomach The Thousandth Floor depends on your squick level when it comes to sibling romance and a heavy drug use. If someone told me before I picked this up that hey, there’s a brother and sister romance here (but they aren’t actually related), I probably wouldn’t have picked it up. As a futuristic Gossip Girl, it lost it’s shine really fast when the character motivations were paper thin and over-dramaticised. While I enjoy a guilty pleasure read as much as the next person, the limited depth in this one just made it drag throughout the book.<br /><br /><i>I received a review copy from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16036143219305528156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2886472405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16239452636819430398"><a href='https://diaryofdifference.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> | <a href='https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> | <a href='https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> | <a href='https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> | <a href='https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2886472405' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thousandth Floor</a> - ★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2960873818' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dazzling Heights</a> - Not Read Yet<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2961335913' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Towering Sky</a> - Not Read Yet <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567409031i/28087046._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In the year 2118, in New York City there’s a thousand-story tower. It has everything you could imagine inside, and there is no need for you to ever get out.<br/><br/>The floor you live on represents your status. The higher you live, the more money you have, which means you become more popular. The rich people don’t necessarily hang around with the poor, an</span>
  <span id="freeText16239452636819430398" style="display:none"><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2886472405" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thousandth Floor</a> - ★★★★<br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2960873818" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dazzling Heights</a> - Not Read Yet<br>#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2961335913" rel="nofollow noopener">The Towering Sky</a> - Not Read Yet <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567409031i/28087046._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the year 2118, in New York City there’s a thousand-story tower. It has everything you could imagine inside, and there is no need for you to ever get out.<br><br>The floor you live on represents your status. The higher you live, the more money you have, which means you become more popular. The rich people don’t necessarily hang around with the poor, and gossips spread faster than lightning. The thousandth floor is the top!<br><br><b>
  <i>But then one night, at a party, one girl falls down from the rooftop of the tower, and the mystery remains – what exactly happened that night? </i>
</b><br><br>Despite all the mixed reviews I’ve seen for this book, I actually really enjoyed it! The world is futuristic and I loved reading about all the different cool items and gadgets that the author was writing about.<br><br>The main character that we have is Avery Fuller, who lives on the thousandth floor of the tower. She has been genetically designed to only have the best genes from her parents, and is, therefore, perfect. But then – SPOILER ALERT – <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she is in love with her brother, who is actually adopted, so not her brother. And as weird as it might seem, they are not related in any way, and the romance was beautifully written. And a lot of you people have been giving this book a bad review because of this reason, but some of you also happen to love ”City of Bones” by Cassandra Clare, who features Clary and Jace, who started with the same background? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Apart from Avery, there were many other characters as well, all of them different and all of them unique at the same time. A girl that works as a main in a rich boy’s house, a girl who is best friends with Avery but doesn’t feel she belongs there, a girl that suddenly finds out she is not rich anymore and has to move onto the lower floors of the tower, a hacker who wants to earn money, no matter the what… The book is written from all these character’s points of view, and I loved the variety and also how all these characters connect to each other in an interesting way. They all have goals, dreams, hopes, fears, and everything is surrounded in drama.<br><br><b>
  <i>If you love Gossip Girl, Pretty Little Liars or the TV Show Riverdale, I guarantee you will enjoy this one. It’s full of mystery, drama, romance, sci-fi and luxury.</i>
</b><br><br>Thank you to my sister, for letting me read this book. I borrowed it from her and will unfortunately have to give it back soon…<br><br><a href="https://diaryofdifference.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/DiaryDifference" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/diaryofdifference/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.co.uk/diaryofdifference/pins/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1788072005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788072005" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788072005?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788072005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1546712430579003845">About: The Thousandth Floor is a young adult dystopian written by Katharine McGee. It was published on 8/30/16 by HarperCollins, 448 pages. The genres are young adult, dystopian, and science fiction. This book is the author’s debut. <br/><br/>My Experience: I started reading The Thousandth Floor on 8/1/17 and finished it on 8/9/17. This book is a great read! There are a lot going on because there are many characters to keep up with. Not only that, the technology in this book is very high tech and out of t</span>
  <span id="freeText1546712430579003845" style="display:none">About: The Thousandth Floor is a young adult dystopian written by Katharine McGee. It was published on 8/30/16 by HarperCollins, 448 pages. The genres are young adult, dystopian, and science fiction. This book is the author’s debut. <br /><br />My Experience: I started reading The Thousandth Floor on 8/1/17 and finished it on 8/9/17. This book is a great read! There are a lot going on because there are many characters to keep up with. Not only that, the technology in this book is very high tech and out of this world. Some are very cool and others are hard for me to imagine, especially how they get from the building to the river to see a comet. It seems like the river is at the tower? I like Watt and his Nadia technology. The stories of the individual characters are interesting. It can be relatable. The Tower sounds very cool.<br /><br />In this book, readers will follow 5 high school students: Leda Cole, Eris Dodd-Radson, Rylin Myers, Watt Bakradi, and Avery Fuller. Leda turns to drugs when the guy she likes left, Eris finds out her life was a lie, Rylin couldn’t be with the guy she loved because of what she did, Watt is a tech genius and does hacking to make extra money, and Avery who is perfect in every way but is still unhappy. They all live at the high rise, The Tower in New York where the higher up you live, the wealthier your family are. This is a futuristic book, therefore, there are high tech in every way, from eartennas to hovercrafts inside the tower. What they have in common is finding someone to love. The wealthy will have a dazzling lifestyles but still struggle with love just as much as the poor who works dead end jobs to pay rent. The wealthy or the poor will turn to drugs when life gets stressed out. Everyone keeps secrets from one another and everyone resents each other thinking that the other has it all. <br /><br />This book is very Gossip Girl style where the rich are spoiled and entitled while the poor struggled to pay bills. The teens are selfish and do what makes them happy. This book is written in third person point of view and readers will get to follow all 5 characters. There is suspense at the end of each chapter for each character. I like following Leda’s train of thoughts. She surprises me the most despite her situations. I like her quick thinking. The ending does leave readers a bit of a cliffhanger. Overall, this book is an interesting read and I do recommend it.<br /><br />Pro: secrets, humor, suspense, multiple point of views,<br /><br />Con: too high tech for my imagination<br /><br />I rate it 4 stars!<br /><br />***Disclaimer: Many thanks to the author Katharine McGee, publisher HarperCollins, and Edelweiss for the opportunity to read and review. I originally lost my access to the ARC and this time I’m reading the finished copy from the library. Please be assured that my opinions are honest.<br /><br />xoxo,<br /> Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14751505641677527565">This wasn't even on my TBR and was a spontaneous read. My library had it. What a fun surprise. The whole <i>Gossip Girl</i> comparison is so apt. I know this is a book I would have to be in the mood for, and I'm glad I was because it was such good brain candy.<br/><br/>It's about the future where rich people live in a thousand floor tower in New York City. The higher the floor where you live, the richer you are. There are parks, aquariums, gardens, malls, schools, everything you can imagine, inside. The characte</span>
  <span id="freeText14751505641677527565" style="display:none">This wasn't even on my TBR and was a spontaneous read. My library had it. What a fun surprise. The whole <i>Gossip Girl</i> comparison is so apt. I know this is a book I would have to be in the mood for, and I'm glad I was because it was such good brain candy.<br /><br />It's about the future where rich people live in a thousand floor tower in New York City. The higher the floor where you live, the richer you are. There are parks, aquariums, gardens, malls, schools, everything you can imagine, inside. The characters are mostly beautiful, in high school, rich, bratty, arrogant, gossiping, drinking/drugging/sexing in cliques. A murder happens at the beginning and we go back through what happens leading up to the event.<br /><br />The book is a perfect vacation or beach or book you can easily read and "guiltily" enjoy. It's a soap opera bigtime. There is a "taboo" romance, one character suddenly becomes "poor" and has to adjust to life in the lower levels. There is LGBTQ rep. You can see in some reviews, readers had some issues, but these things did not bother me and I liked it! Definitely going to read the next one. Hehe<br /><br />A little impromptu buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/828677-you-are-never-too-old-to-young-adult" rel="nofollow noopener">You Are Never Too Old To Young Adult</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1641690801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1641690801" />
    <a title="Izzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy"><img alt="Izzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593145096p2/31211197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1641690801?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Izzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Izzy" href="/user/show/31211197-izzy">Izzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31211197-izzy?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641690801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9045722195024056525">I don't want to sound repetitive, but I have to start this review by saying what pretty much every other reviewer has already said about this book: this is, in a nutshell, futuristic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_' title='Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar' rel='nofollow noopener'> Gossip Girl</a>. And since I devoured that series when I was younger, making it one of my favorites (nope I'm not ashamed), this was a pretty good read for me. It was easy enough to go through, and very quick once you're in the mood for it. But if you're not a fan of reading about petty teenage drama and first world pr</span>
  <span id="freeText9045722195024056525" style="display:none">I don't want to sound repetitive, but I have to start this review by saying what pretty much every other reviewer has already said about this book: this is, in a nutshell, futuristic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gossip Girl</a>. And since I devoured that series when I was younger, making it one of my favorites (nope I'm not ashamed), this was a pretty good read for me. It was easy enough to go through, and very quick once you're in the mood for it. But if you're not a fan of reading about petty teenage drama and first world problems, this will definitely not be the one for you.<br /><br />We follow a cast of five different characters, each with their own questions and problems. There's <b>Avery</b>, the genetically engineered Serena Van der Woodsen of the group, who hails from the richest family and is the most beautiful human in the world but hides some pretty ugly secrets of her own; <b>Leda</b>, who just got off from a stint in rehab and will do anything to keep that part of her life a secret; <b>Eris</b>, who receives unexpected news from her parents that will completely change her life forever; <b>Rylin</b>, whose mom passed away a while ago, forcing her to drop out of school and get a job to keep custody of her little sister; and <b>Watt</b>, who's trying to save for his college fund by performing illegal hacking jobs for people all over the Tower. In the middle of it all, we deal with a drug addiction, drug dealing, some light incest (yeah I know wasn't expecting it either) and money problems. Some of these kids are friends and some of them have never met before, but somehow, all of their problems end up intertangling with each and they gotta find a way out of the mess they created.<br /><br />I'll be honest, some of the storylines were more interesting than others to me, and some characters were just plain annoying. I honestly could not stand Avery and her "woe is me" attitude to life simply because she couldn't be with the boy she loved <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[BECAUSE HE'S HER BROTHER SO IT'S NOT LIKE THAT IS TOO MUCH OF A TRAGEDY <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. She was incredibly selfish but still had this holier than thou air around her simply because, in her eyes, she was the one suffering the most. I honestly just wanted to smack her. But other than her, I actually enjoyed pretty much all the characters, especially Watt and Rylin. In the midst of all the crazyness of the millionaire people, it was nice to see the perspective of two people who couldn't just go on a shopping spree to calm their nerves every time shit went down.<br /><br />And also props to the diversity of this book! <b>It has SUCH a great representation of a variety of characters, in a way I've hardly ever seen before.</b><br /><br />My main problems with this was the lack of worldbuilding, and the sexist attitudes from the male highliers (aka people who live on the highest floors) who went by unnoticed.<br /><br />Seeing as this is a futuristic, slightly sci-fi novel, <b>the reader needs worldbuilding to understand the story better.</b> But absolutely nothing is explained, only briefly mentioned, and I had a really hard time understanding the concept of the Tower. At first I thought the entire city of New York had been transferred to inside the tower, but then at various times there are mentions to characters going outside to visit the rest of the city, like Brooklyn. Does the tower encompass half the city? Just one borough? Why did so many people leave their homes, where they probably led more comfortable, middle-class lives, to live in the lower floors of the Tower in terrible housing? Were they in danger, was there climate change? I thought the construction of the Tower had to do with a heat wave (because climate inside is controlled and at many points, when characters are talking about NY outside the tower, they mention the horrible heat), but then some people go overseas to Paris and Florence and no one mentions anything about climate changes, so... Also, the current currency are ~nanodollars~ and actual paper money is illegal, but does that apply to the people who don't live inside the Tower as well? How do they deal with their finances since they don't have access to as many technological stuff as the people inside? SO MANY QUESTIONS WE DON'T HAVE ANSWERS TO!<br /><br />And in regards to the sexism:<br /><blockquote>
  <b>"Ah," Bryce said quietly, his eyes traveling up and down her body. "Well, I'm glad Cord's taste is improving. You're certainly better than the last one."</b>
</blockquote><br />The rich boys were INCREDIBILY misoginystic at a numbers of times, and NO ONE called them out on it. On the quote I highlighted, I understand why Rylin wouldn't have said anything, because she was, at the time, working as a maid and probably would've gotten in trouble for saying something to the brother of the man who hired her. <u>But she doesn't even think anything about it.</u> She's seen as a piece of meat, clearly harrassed, and she doesn't even exclaim "fuck you" in her head. This happens a number of time throughout the novel; there are plenty of situations where the boys are clearly harrassing and staring at girls like they're made solely for their observation, and they catcall and make gross remarks about them, and the girls say absolutely nothing. There's not even a sentence afterwards that could be interpreted as "hey, this is not actually a nice thing!" They just go on doing their thing like that's normal. <b>It's not. Men don't have the right to stare at girls like they're pieces of meat and exist solely for their gaze.</b> That was a pretty upsetting thing for me.<br /><br />Overall, it was a fun, fast-paced, light book. Definitely recommend reading it if you're tired of heavier books and just needs something quick to get through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9045722195024056525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1726522523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1726522523" />
    <a title="Sail ♛ A Wicked Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56414354-sail-a-wicked-reader"><img alt="Sail ♛ A Wicked Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558116920p2/56414354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1726522523?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sail ♛ A Wicked Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sail ♛ A Wicked Reader" href="/user/show/56414354-sail-a-wicked-reader">Sail ♛ A Wicked Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062418593" href="/book/show/28218953-the-thousandth-floor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56414354-sail-a-wicked-reader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726522523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4108746165627324097"><b>If you liked the show Gossip Girl, then you will definitely love this.</b><br/><br/>Going into this, I didn't really know much about it other than the fact that it's set in the future and follows the story of 5 teenagers. My expectations weren't that high for it either, but it ended up blowing me away. This is Katharine McGee's debut novel but it was written as if she is a seasoned author. She clearly has a talent for writing and her style really captivates you. After reading the very first page, I knew that </span>
  <span id="freeText4108746165627324097" style="display:none"><b>If you liked the show Gossip Girl, then you will definitely love this.</b><br /><br />Going into this, I didn't really know much about it other than the fact that it's set in the future and follows the story of 5 teenagers. My expectations weren't that high for it either, but it ended up blowing me away. This is Katharine McGee's debut novel but it was written as if she is a seasoned author. She clearly has a talent for writing and her style really captivates you. After reading the very first page, I knew that I was going to love this story.<br /><br /><i>The Thousandth Floor</i> is set in the year 2118 in none other than New York City. The Tower is an unimaginable large building that everyone lives in, works in, goes to school, and everything else. Each floor consists of neighborhoods, schools, restaurants, etc. Basically each floor is so gigantic, that it's like a mini-city on each floor. There's no need to leave the Tower at all. There are 1,000 total floors in the building. The higher floors are for the wealthy only, called highliers. The lower floors are for the poorer people. Everything is super futuristic and the technology is amazing. There aren't cell phones anymore. People wear contacts that allow them to see their messages and social media. Retina scanners above front doors let you in instead of having to use keys.<br /><br />The story is narrated by 5 different teenagers whom live in the Tower and they all lead very different lives. Yet their stories all come together at the end.<br />Avery lives on the 1,00th floor, which means that she's the richest and the most popular. She's also the most beautiful, and everyone either wants to be her or be with her. But Avery is hiding a dark secret from everyone..<br />Eris is a highlier as well, and she comes from very old money. She's also friends with Avery, and she's that girl that has had a fling with pretty much everyone. She is also a bisexual character. But something happens that wrecks Eris's world.<br />Leda is yet another highlier, and is best friends with Avery. She's just returned from rehab after becoming addicted to drugs due to her party-filled life. But the reason that Leda started using drugs is back, and she starts to lose control of her life again.<br />Watt is a downlier. He lives on the 240th floor and his family is really struggling with money. So he creates an illegal supercomputer and does jobs on the side for more money. But he begins struggling once he's brought into the crazy life of the highliers.<br />Rylin lives on the 32nd floor and is the poorest of them all. Her parents are gone so she was forced to drop out of school and get a job in order to take care of her younger sister. But her life gets crazy when her boyfriend deals drugs, and she starts working for a highlier.<br /><br />All of the characters, including the huge group of minor characters, were totally enjoyable. Rylin and Cord were my favorites, but they were all great and written very well.<br /><br />GRADING SCALE<br />Characters - 18/20<br />Plot line - 13/15<br />Originality - 15/15<br />Writing Style - 15/15<br />Pace - 14/15<br />Ending - 15/15<br />Total = 90/100<br />5/5 stars<br /><br /><b>It's a story full of partying, lies, deceit, scandals, drama, romance, and so much more. Like I said, it's kind of like a very futuristic version of Gossip Girl.<br /><br /><i>The Thousandth Floor</i> was an excellent story, and I would gladly recommend it to others. I need the next book right now.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4108746165627324097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It tried hard to be great, but unintentionally fell far, far, down into a messy and completely shit splattered mess. <br/><br/>This book killed off its <b>ONLY</b> redeeming character.   <b>
    <i>FOR SOME REASON, I NEVER RATED THIS BUT I FINISHED IT IN 2016????!!!!!!</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />OK first of all, this book is like a much lesser version of <i>Gossip Girl</i>. It tried hard to be great, but unintentionally fell far, far, down into a messy and completely shit splattered mess. <br /><br />This book killed off its <b>ONLY</b> redeeming character. A character that was probably the most developed and interesting AND <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>a person who was BISEXUAL</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />WHAT THE FUCK. <br />I was completely irritated and frustrated at the ending. <br />Utter bullshit. <br /><br />I remember the day I finished this book (at work on a lunch break) and I was soooooo fucking bitter; it was <i>not</i> a good day. I snapped at people and wanted to stew in 'how-the-fuck-did-this-just-happen'. <br /><br />Easily mindless entertainment and drama to say in the least, but every time I think how unjustly the only character I liked in this dumb book was killed.....<br /><br /><br /><i>

<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_49246699'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49246699-the-heir-affair"><img alt="The Heir Affair (Royal We, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1571697145l/49246699._SX98_SY160_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GTMxdfTvmOzndznOwYRzWfT/W2soSxlHOrayCG1yGS+sgt1mwFFW/yMuJSQm2wDr4O3wFLWNXMLisPkwWlYDXA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tgCTgepht9saP0S/xvS1XhL1IfgIeElbyFub0Ck/TXMDsX+S3t95yN5mWFUhq8bsBueKh5W+DN4QXdDoHhtXAA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8171810218535504669">Katharine McGee is the New York Times bestselling author of American Royals and The Thousandth Floor trilogy. She studied English and French literature at Princeton University and has an MBA from Stanford. She lives in her hometown of Houston, TX with her husband.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_36039298').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_36039298').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_36039298').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
